     4â†’---
     5â†’
     6â†’# Steno: Stenographic Command Interface
     7â†’
     8â†’You understand and execute stenographic shorthand for efficient coding and data analysis.
     9â†’
    10â†’## Recognition
    11â†’
    12â†’Execute steno commands when you see this pattern:
    13â†’```
    14â†’[mode][verb]:[target] [@refs] [+additions] [-exclusions] [.flags] [precision]
    15â†’```
    16â†’
    17â†’**Trigger patterns:**
    18â†’- `verb:target` (e.g., `dx:@file.csv`, `mk:api`, `ch:login`)
    19â†’- `verb:type @file` (e.g., `viz:pca @data.csv`, `stat:ttest @a @b`)
    20â†’- `?mode topic` (e.g., `?plan architecture`, `?sketch auth-flow`)
    21â†’- Commands ending in `~deep` or `~` or `!` or `?`
    22â†’- `steno:command` (session management commands)
    23â†’
    24â†’## Core Verbs
    25â†’
    26â†’| Verb | Meaning | Action |
    27â†’|------|---------|--------|
    28â†’| `dx` | Diagnose/explore | Read, analyze, summarize |
    29â†’| `mk` | Make/create | Create new file, component, feature |
    30â†’| `ch` | Change/modify | Edit existing code |
    31â†’| `rm` | Remove/delete | Delete code, files, features |
    32â†’| `fnd` | Find/search | Search codebase |
    33â†’| `viz` | Visualize | Generate visualization or analysis |
    34â†’| `stat` | Statistics | Run statistical test or analysis |
    35â†’| `ts` | Test | Run or create tests |
    36â†’| `doc` | Document | Generate documentation |
    37â†’
    38â†’## Modifiers
    39â†’
    40â†’| Syntax | Meaning | Example |
    41â†’|--------|---------|---------|
    42â†’| `@file.ext` | File reference | `dx:@data.csv` |
    43â†’| `@name` | Named reference or bookmark | `ch:@auth-module` |
    44â†’| `+feature` | Add/include | `mk:api +auth +cache` |
    45â†’| `-thing` | Exclude/without | `ch:@config -logging` |
    46â†’| `.flag` | Apply flag | `.ts` (TypeScript), `.dry` (dry run) |
    47â†’| `.flag:value` | Flag with qualifier | `.plot:png`, `.ts:edge` |
    48â†’
    49â†’## Precision Markers
    50â†’
    51â†’| Marker | Meaning | Your behavior |
    52â†’|--------|---------|---------------|
    53â†’| `~` | Flexible | Use your judgment |
    54â†’| `!` | Exact/literal | Do exactly what's specified |
    55â†’| `?` | Clarify | Ask before acting |
    56â†’| `~deep` | Extended thinking | Think deeply, consider alternatives |
    57â†’

    68â†’
    69â†’## Session Tracking
    70â†’
    71â†’Steno tracks commands in `.steno/` for cross-session memory and stale detection.
    72â†’
    73â†’### On Session Start
    74â†’
    75â†’When you first see a steno command in a session:
    76â†’
    77â†’1. Check if `.steno/graph.json` exists
    78â†’2. If yes, briefly note the last session:
    79â†’   ```
    80â†’   > Previous session (Dec 26, 3 commands)
    81â†’   > Last: viz:pca @normalized.csv
    82â†’   ```
    83â†’3. Check for stale outputs (files that changed since commands ran)
    84â†’
    85â†’### After Each Command
    86â†’
    87â†’After executing a steno command, log it to `.steno/current-session.json`:
    88â†’
    89â†’1. Read the file (create if missing, with empty `nodes` array)
    90â†’2. Determine the next node ID from the file or start at `n_001`
    91â†’3. Append a node:
    92â†’   ```json
    93â†’   {
    94â†’     "id": "n_001",
    95â†’     "timestamp": "2024-12-27T14:30:22Z",
    96â†’     "raw": "dx:@samples.csv",
    97â†’     "status": "complete",
    98â†’     "inputs": ["samples.csv"],
    99â†’     "outputs": [],
   100â†’     "summary": "18 samples, 5 genes, 2 conditions"
   101â†’   }
   102â†’   ```
   103â†’4. Write back to the file
   104â†’
   105â†’### Node Structure
   106â†’
   107â†’```json
   108â†’{
   109â†’  "id": "n_001",
   110â†’  "timestamp": "ISO timestamp",
   111â†’  "raw": "the original command",
   112â†’  "status": "complete|failed",
   113â†’  "inputs": ["files read"],
   114â†’  "outputs": ["files created or modified"],
   115â†’  "summary": "brief description of result"
   116â†’}
   117â†’```
   118â†’
   119â†’### Tracking Inputs/Outputs
   120â†’
   121â†’- **Inputs**: Files explicitly referenced (`@file`) plus any files you read
   122â†’- **Outputs**: Files you create or modify
   123â†’- **Summary**: One-line description of the result
   124â†’
   125â†’---
   126â†’
   127â†’## Reference Resolution
   128â†’
   129â†’### The `^` Reference (Previous Output)
   130â†’
   131â†’When you see `^` in a command:
   132â†’
   133â†’1. Read `.steno/current-session.json`
   134â†’2. Find the last node
   135â†’3. Use its outputs as input for this command
   136â†’
   137â†’Example:
   138â†’```
   139â†’dx:@samples.csv           # outputs: analyzed samples.csv
   140â†’ch:^ +normalize           # ^ = samples.csv from previous
   141â†’viz:pca ^                 # ^ = normalized output from previous
   142â†’```
   143â†’
   144â†’If the previous node has no outputs, use its inputs.
   145â†’
   146â†’### The `@name` Reference (Bookmark)
   147â†’
   148â†’When you see `@name` that isn't a file path:
   149â†’
   150â†’1. Check if it's a file that exists - if so, use the file
   151â†’2. Otherwise, check `.steno/graph.json` bookmarks
   152â†’3. If found, resolve to that node's outputs
   153â†’
   154â†’Example:
   155â†’```

   157â†’# @baseline-pca resolves to outputs of bookmarked node
   158â†’# @new-samples is a file reference
   159â†’```
   160â†’
   161â†’---
   162â†’

Assistant2025-12-28T02:28:37.109Z




$ Bash


Generate heatmap visualization
python3 -c "
import pandas as pd
import matplotlib.pyplot as plt
import seaborn as sns

# Read data
df = pd.read_csv('examples/vignette/samples.csv')

# Create sample labels with condition info
df['label'] = df['treatment'] + '_' + df['timepoint']

# Extract gene columns for heatmap
genes = ['gene_A', 'gene_B', 'gene_C', 'gene_D', 'gene_E']
heatmap_data = df[genes].copy()
heatmap_data.index = df['sample_id'] + ' (' + df['label'] + ')'

# Sort by treatment then timepoint for better visualization
df['time_order'] = df['timepoint'].map({'0h': 0, '24h': 1, '48h': 2})
df['trt_order'] = df['treatment'].map({'control': 0, 'treatment': 1})
sort_idx = df.sort_values(['trt_order', 'time_order']).index
heatmap_data = heatmap_data.iloc[sort_idx]

# Create figure
fig, ax = plt.subplots(figsize=(10, 8))
sns.heatmap(heatmap_data, annot=True, fmt='.2f', cmap='YlOrRd', 
            cbar_kws={'label': 'Expression'}, ax=ax)
ax.set_title('Gene Expression Heatmap\\n(sorted by treatment & timepoint)')
ax.set_xlabel('Genes')
ax.set_ylabel('Samples')
plt.tight_layout()
plt.savefig('examples/vignette/heatmap.png', dpi=150)
print('Saved: examples/vignette/heatmap.png')
"

Assistant2025-12-28T02:31:02.668Z




$ Bash


Generate clustered heatmap
python3 -c "
import pandas as pd
import matplotlib.pyplot as plt
import seaborn as sns

# Read data
df = pd.read_csv('examples/vignette/samples.csv')

# Create sample labels with condition info
df['label'] = df['treatment'] + '_' + df['timepoint']

# Extract gene columns for heatmap
genes = ['gene_A', 'gene_B', 'gene_C', 'gene_D', 'gene_E']
heatmap_data = df[genes].copy()
heatmap_data.index = df['sample_id'] + ' (' + df['label'] + ')'

# Create clustered heatmap
g = sns.clustermap(heatmap_data, annot=True, fmt='.2f', cmap='YlOrRd',
                   figsize=(10, 10), cbar_kws={'label': 'Expression'},
                   row_cluster=True, col_cluster=True,
                   dendrogram_ratio=(0.15, 0.15))
g.fig.suptitle('Clustered Gene Expression Heatmap', y=1.02)
plt.savefig('examples/vignette/heatmap_clustered.png', dpi=150, bbox_inches='tight')
print('Saved: examples/vignette/heatmap_clustered.png')
"
